<h2> Timeline of Roman history</h2>

<h2><span id="8th_and_7th_centuries_BC" class="mw-headline">8th and 7th centuries BC</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%&rdquo;">

<th>Event</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="753 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/753_BC">753&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>21 April</td>
<td><a title="Founding of Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_of_Rome">Rome was founded</a>. According to Roman legend,&nbsp;<a title="Romulus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romulus">Romulus</a>&nbsp;was the founder and first&nbsp;<a title="King of Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Rome">King of Rome</a>, establishing the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Kingdom">Roman Kingdom</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="715 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/715_BC">715&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Numa Pompilius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numa_Pompilius">Numa Pompilius</a>&nbsp;became the second King of Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="673 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/673_BC">673&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Tullus Hostilius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tullus_Hostilius">Tullus Hostilius</a>&nbsp;became the third King of Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="667 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/667_BC">667&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Byzantium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantium">Byzantium</a>&nbsp;was founded by&nbsp;<a title="Megara" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megara">Megarian</a>&nbsp;colonists.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="Tullus Hostilius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tullus_Hostilius">Tullus Hostilius</a>&nbsp;died.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The Curiate Assembly, one of the&nbsp;<a title="Legislative Assemblies of the Roman Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legislative_Assemblies_of_the_Roman_Kingdom">legislative assemblies of the Roman Kingdom</a>, elected&nbsp;<a title="Ancus Marcius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancus_Marcius">Ancus Marcius</a>&nbsp;King of Rome.</td>

<h2><span id="6th_century_BC" class="mw-headline">6th century BC</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Date</th>
<th>Event</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="575 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/575_BC">575&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Senate of the Roman Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senate_of_the_Roman_Kingdom">Senate</a>&nbsp;accepted the&nbsp;<a title="Regent" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regent">regent</a>&nbsp;<a title="Servius Tullius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Servius_Tullius">Servius Tullius</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<a title="King of Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Rome">king</a>&nbsp;of Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="535 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/535_BC">535&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Servius Tullius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Servius_Tullius">Servius Tullius</a>&nbsp;was murdered by his daughter&nbsp;<a title="Tullia Minor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tullia_Minor">Tullia Minor</a>&nbsp;and her husband&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus">Lucius Tarquinius Superbus</a>, who declared himself King of Rome on the steps of the&nbsp;<em><a title="Curia Hostilia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curia_Hostilia">Curia Hostilia</a></em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="5" valign="top"><a title="509 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/509_BC">509&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Patrician (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)">patrician</a>&nbsp;<a title="Lucretia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucretia">Lucretia</a>&nbsp;was raped by&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus">Lucius Tarquinius Superbus'</a>&nbsp;son&nbsp;<a title="Sextus Tarquinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sextus_Tarquinius">Sextus Tarquinius</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Overthrow of the Roman monarchy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Roman_monarchy">Overthrow of the Roman monarchy</a></em>: Following&nbsp;<a title="Lucretia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucretia">Lucretia's</a>&nbsp;suicide,&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Junius Brutus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Junius_Brutus">Lucius Junius Brutus</a>&nbsp;called the Curiate Assembly, one of the&nbsp;<a title="Legislative Assemblies of the Roman Kingdom" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legislative_Assemblies_of_the_Roman_Kingdom">legislative assemblies of the Roman Kingdom</a>. The latter agreed to the overthrow and expulsion of&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus">Lucius Tarquinius Superbus</a>&nbsp;and to a provisional constitution under which two&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consuls</a>&nbsp;acted as a joint&nbsp;<a title="Executive (government)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_(government)">executive</a>&nbsp;and a&nbsp;<a title="Curiate Assembly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curiate_Assembly">Curiate Assembly</a>&nbsp;held legislative power, and swore never again to let a&nbsp;<a title="King of Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Rome">king</a>&nbsp;rule Rome. It further elected Lucius Junius Brutus and&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Collatinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Collatinus">Lucius Tarquinius Collatinus</a>, Lucretia's husband, as consuls.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Silva Arsia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Silva_Arsia">Battle of Silva Arsia</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Tarquinia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarquinia">Tarquinian</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Veii" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veii">Veientine</a>&nbsp;forces loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus">Lucius Tarquinius Superbus</a>&nbsp;were defeated in the&nbsp;<a title="Silva Arsia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silva_Arsia">Silva Arsia</a>&nbsp;by a Roman army.&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Junius Brutus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Junius_Brutus">Lucius Junius Brutus</a>&nbsp;was killed.&nbsp;<a title="Publius Valerius Publicola" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Valerius_Publicola">Publius Valerius Publicola</a>, returning to Rome with the spoils of war, was awarded the first&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Triumph" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Triumph">Roman Triumph</a>&nbsp;on March 1.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>&nbsp;<a title="Publius Valerius Publicola" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Valerius_Publicola">Publius Valerius Publicola</a>&nbsp;promulgated a number of liberal reforms, including opening the office of consul to all Roman citizens and placing the treasury under the administration of appointed&nbsp;<a title="Quaestor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaestor">quaestors</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>13 September</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_of_Jupiter_Optimus_Maximus">Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus</a>&nbsp;was ceremonially dedicated to the&nbsp;<a title="Capitoline Triad" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitoline_Triad">Capitoline Triad</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="508 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/508_BC">508&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Roman&ndash;Etruscan Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Etruscan_Wars">Roman&ndash;Etruscan Wars</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Clusium" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clusium">Clusian</a>&nbsp;army failed to conquer&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="501 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/501_BC">501&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>In the face of a potential&nbsp;<a title="Sabines" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabines">Sabine</a>&nbsp;invasion, the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;passed a&nbsp;<em><a title="Senatus consultum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senatus_consultum">senatus consultum</a></em>&nbsp;authorizing the&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consuls</a>&nbsp;to appoint a&nbsp;<a title="Roman dictator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_dictator">dictator</a>, a magistrate who held absolute power during a national emergency. The dictator would in turn appoint the&nbsp;<em><a title="Magister equitum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magister_equitum">Magister equitum</a></em>, the commander of the&nbsp;<a title="Roman cavalry" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_cavalry">cavalry</a>. The consuls&nbsp;<a title="Titus Lartius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titus_Lartius">Titus Lartius</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Postumus Cominius Auruncus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Postumus_Cominius_Auruncus">Postumus Cominius Auruncus</a>&nbsp;selected the former as dictator.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h2><span id="5th_century_BC" class="mw-headline">5th century BC</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Date</th>
<th>Event</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="496 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/496_BC">496&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Lake Regillus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_Regillus">Battle of Lake Regillus</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Latin League" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_League">Latin League</a>&nbsp;invasion near modern&nbsp;<a title="Frascati" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frascati">Frascati</a>&nbsp;which sought to reinstall&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus">Lucius Tarquinius Superbus</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="494 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/494_BC">494&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="First secessio plebis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_secessio_plebis"><em>First</em>&nbsp;secessio plebis</a>:
<p><a title="Lucius Sicinius Vellutus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Sicinius_Vellutus">Lucius Sicinius Vellutus</a>, the&nbsp;<em><a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebs</a></em>&nbsp;abandoned&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>&nbsp;for the nearby&nbsp;<a title="Monte Sacro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monte_Sacro">Monte Sacro</a>.</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="471 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/471_BC">471&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>After a law allowing organization of the&nbsp;<em><a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebs</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Roman tribe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_tribe">tribe</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Plebeian Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebeian_Council">Plebeian Council</a>&nbsp;was reorganized by tribes rather than&nbsp;<a title="Curia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curia">curiae</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="459 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/459_BC">459&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>Under popular pressure, the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;increased the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Tribune of the Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribune_of_the_Plebs">tribunes of the&nbsp;<em>plebs</em></a>&nbsp;from two to ten.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="458 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/458_BC">458&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>During the first dictatorship of&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnatus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cincinnatus">Cincinnatus</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Aequi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aequi">Aequians</a>&nbsp;staged an offensive, breaking a truce. Cincinnatus defeated the Aquians at the&nbsp;<a title="Battle of Mount Algidus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mount_Algidus">Battle of Mount Algidus</a>&nbsp;and after a triumph, returned to his farm after sixteen days.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="449 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/449_BC">449&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>Resolutions of the&nbsp;<a title="Plebeian Council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebeian_Council">Plebeian Council</a>&nbsp;were given the full force of law subject to&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;veto.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The second of two&nbsp;<a title="Decemviri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decemviri">decemviri</a>, specially-elected ten man commissions, issued the last of the&nbsp;<a title="Twelve Tables" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twelve_Tables">Twelve Tables</a>, the fundamental laws of the Republic.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="447 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/447_BC">447&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Tribal Assembly" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_Assembly">Tribal Assembly</a>&nbsp;was established, and granted the right to elect&nbsp;<a title="Quaestor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaestor">quaestors</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="445 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/445_BC">445&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Lex Canuleia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lex_Canuleia">Lex Canuleia</a>:</em>&nbsp;Marriage between&nbsp;<a title="Patrician (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)">patricians</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeians</a>&nbsp;was legalized.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="443 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/443_BC">443&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The offices of the&nbsp;<em><a title="Tribuni militum consulari potestate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribuni_militum_consulari_potestate">Tribuni militum consulari potestate</a></em>&nbsp;were established. A&nbsp;<a title="Collegium (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collegium_(ancient_Rome)">collegium</a>&nbsp;of three&nbsp;<a title="Patrician (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)">patrician</a>&nbsp;or&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Tribune" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribune">tribunes</a>, one each from specific&nbsp;<a title="Roman tribe" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_tribe">Roman tribes</a>&nbsp;(the Titienses, the Ramnenses, and the Luceres), would hold the power of the&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consuls</a>&nbsp;from year to year, subject to the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The office of the&nbsp;<a title="Roman censor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_censor">censor</a>, a&nbsp;<a title="Patrician (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)">patrician</a>&nbsp;magistrate responsible for conducting the&nbsp;<a title="Census" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Census">census</a>&nbsp;in years without a&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>, was established.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="439 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/439_BC">439&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>Cincinnatus was called upon to accept a second dictatorship by the patricians to prevent&nbsp;<a title="Spurius Maelius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spurius_Maelius">Spurius Maelius</a>&nbsp;from seizing power; the patricians suspected Spurius of using wheat to purchase the support of the plebeians, to set himself up as a king.&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Servilius Ahala" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Servilius_Ahala">Gaius Servilius Ahala</a>&nbsp;was appointed&nbsp;<a title="Magister equitum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magister_equitum">magister equitum</a>&nbsp;in order to stop Maelius; following an attack by Maelius, Ahala slew him. Cincinnatus again resigned his dictatorship and returned to his farm after 21 days.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="435 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/435_BC">435&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Capture of Fidenae (435 BC)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capture_of_Fidenae_(435_BC)">Fidenae</a>, an important trade post on the Tiber, was captured from the Veii.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="408 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/408_BC">408&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<em><a title="Tribuni militum consulari potestate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribuni_militum_consulari_potestate">Tribuni militum consulari potestate</a></em>&nbsp;held office.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h2><span id="4th_century_BC" class="mw-headline">4th century BC</span></h2>
<table class="wikitable" width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Date</th>
<th>Event</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="396 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/396_BC">396&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Veii" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Veii">Battle of Veii</a></em>: Roman forces led by the&nbsp;<a title="Roman dictator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_dictator">dictator</a>&nbsp;<a title="Marcus Furius Camillus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Furius_Camillus">Marcus Furius Camillus</a>&nbsp;conquered&nbsp;<a title="Veii" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veii">Veii</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>Roman soldiers first earned a salary ("salary" from Latin for "salt").</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="390 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/390_BC">390&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>18 July</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of the Allia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Allia">Battle of the Allia</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Senones" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senones">Senones</a>&nbsp;routed a Roman force at the confluence of the rivers&nbsp;<a title="Allia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allia">Allia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Tiber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiber">Tiber</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Senones" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senones">Senones</a>&nbsp;sacked&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>. Among other artifacts, books were destroyed. The history of Rome up to this point had to be mostly reconstructed and is sometimes unreliable or mythological.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="367 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/367_BC">367&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>

<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consuls</a>&nbsp;held office.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="366 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/366_BC">366&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" title="Lucius Sextius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Sextius">Lucius Sextius</a>&nbsp;was elected the first&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The office of&nbsp;<em><a title="Praetor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetor">Praetor</a></em>, which took the&nbsp;<a title="Judiciary" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judiciary">judiciary</a>&nbsp;responsibilities of the&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>&nbsp;and could be held only by a&nbsp;<a title="Patrician (ancient Rome)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)">patrician</a>, was established.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="351 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/351_BC">351&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The first&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roman dictator" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_dictator">dictator</a>&nbsp;was elected.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The first&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roman censor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_censor">censor</a>&nbsp;was elected.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="343 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/343_BC">343&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Samnite Wars" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samnite_Wars">Samnite Wars</a></em>: Rome marched against the&nbsp;<a title="Samnites" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samnites">Samnites</a>, probably after an appeal from the&nbsp;<a title="Campanians" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campanians">Campanians</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Mount Gaurus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mount_Gaurus">Battle of Mount Gaurus</a></em>: A&nbsp;<a title="Samnites" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samnites">Samnite</a>&nbsp;force was routed by a Roman army near&nbsp;<a title="Mount Barbaro" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mount_Barbaro">Mount Barbaro</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="342 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/342_BC">342&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<em><a title="Leges Genuciae" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leges_Genuciae">Leges Genuciae</a></em>&nbsp;were passed, banning a person from holding two offices at the same time, or during any ten-year period; charging interest on loans was also banned.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="341 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/341_BC">341&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Samnite Wars</em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;agreed a peace, following an appeal by the&nbsp;<a title="Samnites" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samnites">Samnite</a>&nbsp;to a previous treaty of friendship.</td>
</tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="339 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/339_BC">339&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>A law was passed which required the election of at least one&nbsp;<a title="Plebs" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plebs">plebeian</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roman censor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_censor">censor</a>&nbsp;every five years.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Lautulae" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Lautulae">Battle of Lautulae</a></em>: A decisive&nbsp;<a title="Samnites" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samnites">Samnite</a>&nbsp;victory near&nbsp;<a title="Terracina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terracina">Terracina</a>&nbsp;split Roman territory in two.</td>

The&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>&nbsp;<a title="Publius Decius Mus (consul 312 BC)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Decius_Mus_(consul_312_BC)">Publius Decius Mus (consul 312 BC)</a>&nbsp;was killed.</td>

The&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Atilius Regulus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Atilius_Regulus">Gaius Atilius Regulus</a>&nbsp;was killed.</td>

<td><a title="101 BC" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/101_BC">101&nbsp;<small>BC</small></a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Vercellae" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Vercellae">Battle of Vercellae</a></em>: An invasion of Italy by the&nbsp;<a title="Cimbri" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cimbri">Cimbri</a>&nbsp;was decisively defeated by a numerically inferior Roman force. Some hundred thousand Cimbri soldiers and civilians were killed along with their king&nbsp;<a title="Boiorix" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boiorix">Boiorix</a>.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

<td><a title="Gaius Marius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Marius">Marius</a>&nbsp;was elected&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>.</td>

<td>10 December</td>
<td>Assassins hired by&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Marius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Marius">Marius</a>'s political allies&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Appuleius Saturninus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Appuleius_Saturninus">Lucius Appuleius Saturninus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Servilius Glaucia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Servilius_Glaucia">Gaius Servilius Glaucia</a>&nbsp;beat to death&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Memmius (tribune)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Memmius_(tribune)">Gaius Memmius</a>, a candidate for the&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consulship</a>.</td>

<td>30 August</td>
<td><a title="Cleopatra" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleopatra">Cleopatra</a>&nbsp;committed suicide, probably in Roman custody and by snakebite.</td>

<td><a title="Augustus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus">Augustus</a>&nbsp;indicated his nephew&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Claudius Marcellus (Julio-Claudian dynasty)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Claudius_Marcellus_(Julio-Claudian_dynasty)">Marcus Claudius Marcellus (Julio-Claudian dynasty)</a>&nbsp;as his chosen successor by marrying him to his only daughter&nbsp;<a title="Julia the Elder" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julia_the_Elder">Julia the Elder</a>.</td>

<td><em><a title="Battle of the Teutoburg Forest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Teutoburg_Forest">Battle of the Teutoburg Forest</a></em>: A coalition of&nbsp;<a title="Germanic peoples" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_peoples">Germanic</a>&nbsp;forces ambushed and destroyed three Roman&nbsp;<a title="Roman legion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_legion">legions</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Teutoburg Forest" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teutoburg_Forest">Teutoburg Forest</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Publius Quinctilius Varus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Publius_Quinctilius_Varus">Publius Quinctilius Varus</a>, the commander of Roman forces in&nbsp;<a title="Germania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germania">Germania</a>, committed suicide.</td>

His son&nbsp;<a title="Sejanus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sejanus">Sejanus</a>&nbsp;remained as the sole&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian prefect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_prefect">prefect</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian Guard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_Guard">Praetorian Guard</a>.</td>

<td><a title="AD 19" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_19"><small>AD</small>&nbsp;19</a></td>
<td>10 October</td>
<td><a title="Germanicus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanicus">Germanicus</a>&nbsp;died in&nbsp;<a title="Antioch" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antioch">Antioch</a>, possibly after being poisoned on&nbsp;<a title="Tiberius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberius">Tiberius's</a>&nbsp;orders.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="AD 22" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_22"><small>AD</small>&nbsp;22</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Tiberius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberius">Tiberius</a>&nbsp;granted&nbsp;<a title="Drusus Julius Caesar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drusus_Julius_Caesar">Drusus Julius Caesar</a>&nbsp;<a title="Tribune" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribune">tribunician</a>&nbsp;power, marking him as his choice as successor.</td>

His will left his offices jointly to&nbsp;<a title="Caligula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caligula">Caligula</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Drusus Julius Caesar" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drusus_Julius_Caesar">Drusus Julius Caesar's</a>&nbsp;son, his grandson&nbsp;<a title="Tiberius Gemellus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiberius_Gemellus">Tiberius Gemellus</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Ptolemy of Mauretania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ptolemy_of_Mauretania">Ptolemy of Mauretania</a>,&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Mauretania" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauretania">Mauretania</a>&nbsp;and a Roman&nbsp;<a title="Client state" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Client_state">client</a>, was murdered on&nbsp;<a title="Caligula" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caligula">Caligula's</a>&nbsp;orders during a state visit to&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>. His slave&nbsp;<a title="Aedemon" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aedemon">Aedemon</a>&nbsp;rose in revolt against Roman rule.</td>

<td rowspan="3" valign="top"><a title="AD 68" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_68"><small>AD</small>&nbsp;68</a></td>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">9 June</td>
<td><a title="Nero" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nero">Nero</a>, then in hiding in the villa of the&nbsp;<a title="Freedman" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedman">freedman</a>&nbsp;<a title="Phaon (freedman)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phaon_(freedman)">Phaon (freedman)</a>, was notified that the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;had declared him an enemy of the state and ordered him brought to the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Forum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Forum">Forum</a>&nbsp;to be publicly beaten to death. He ordered his secretary&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Epaphroditos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epaphroditos">Epaphroditos</a>&nbsp;to kill him.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;accepted&nbsp;<a title="Galba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galba">Galba</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Roman governor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_governor">governor</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Hispania Tarraconensis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis">Hispania Tarraconensis</a>, as ruler of Rome.</td>

<td><em><a title="Zealot Temple Siege" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zealot_Temple_Siege">Zealot Temple Siege</a></em>: The forces of&nbsp;<a title="Ananus ben Ananus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ananus_ben_Ananus">Ananus ben Ananus</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Jewish</a>&nbsp;former&nbsp;<a title="High Priest of Israel" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_Priest_of_Israel">High Priest of Israel</a>, laid siege to the&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Zealots (Judea)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zealots_(Judea)">Zealots</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Second Temple" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Temple">Second Temple</a>.</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>16 April</td>
<td>Following his defeat by&nbsp;<a title="Vitellius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitellius">Vitellius</a>, the commander of the Roman army on the lower&nbsp;<a title="Rhine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhine">Rhine</a>, near modern&nbsp;<a title="Calvatone" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calvatone">Calvatone</a>, and to prevent further civil war,&nbsp;<a title="Otho" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Otho">Otho</a>&nbsp;committed suicide.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Revolt of the Batavi" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Batavi">Revolt of the Batavi</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Julius Civilis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Julius_Civilis">Gaius Julius Civilis</a>, commander of the&nbsp;<a title="Batavi (Germanic tribe)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Batavi_(Germanic_tribe)">Batavi</a>&nbsp;auxiliaries in the&nbsp;<a title="Rhine" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhine">Rhine</a>&nbsp;<a title="Roman legion" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_legion">legions</a>, turned against Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>December</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;recognized&nbsp;<a title="Vespasian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vespasian">Vespasian</a>, the commander of Roman forces in&nbsp;<a title="Egypt (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt_(Roman_province)">Egypt</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Judea (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea_(Roman_province)">Judea</a>, as ruler of Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>22 December</td>
<td><a title="Vitellius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitellius">Vitellius</a>&nbsp;was executed in&nbsp;<a title="Rome" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rome">Rome</a>&nbsp;by troops loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Vespasian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vespasian">Vespasian</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="AD 70" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_70"><small>AD</small>&nbsp;70</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Revolt of the Batavi</em>: Following a series of battlefield reversals,&nbsp;<a title="Gaius Julius Civilis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaius_Julius_Civilis">Civilis</a>&nbsp;accepted peace terms from the Roman&nbsp;<a title="General officer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_officer">general</a>&nbsp;<a title="Quintus Petillius Cerialis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quintus_Petillius_Cerialis">Quintus Petillius Cerialis</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>September</td>
<td><em><a title="Siege of Jerusalem (70 CE)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Jerusalem_(70_CE)">Siege of Jerusalem (70 CE)</a></em>: The Roman&nbsp;<a title="General officer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_officer">general</a>&nbsp;<a title="Titus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Titus">Titus</a>&nbsp;breached the walls of&nbsp;<a title="Jerusalem" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, sacked the city and destroyed the&nbsp;<a title="Second Temple" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Temple">Second Temple</a>.</td>

<td><em><a title="Siege of Masada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Masada">Siege of Masada</a></em>: Roman forces breached the walls of&nbsp;<a title="Masada" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masada">Masada</a>, a mountain fortress held by the&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Jewish</a>&nbsp;extremist sect the&nbsp;<a title="Sicarii" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicarii">Sicarii</a>.</td>

<td><a title="AD 132" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_132">132</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Bar Kokhba revolt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_Kokhba_revolt">Bar Kokhba revolt</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Simon bar Kokhba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_bar_Kokhba">Simon bar Kokhba</a>, believed by his followers to be the&nbsp;<a title="Messiah in Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messiah_in_Judaism">Messiah</a>, launched a revolt against Roman authority in&nbsp;<a title="Judea (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea_(Roman_province)">Judea</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="AD 135" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_135">135</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Bar Kokhba revolt</em>: The revolt ended at a cost of tens of thousands of Roman soldiers and some six hundred thousand&nbsp;<a title="Judaism" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism">Jewish</a>&nbsp;rebels and civilians, including&nbsp;<a title="Simon bar Kokhba" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_bar_Kokhba">bar Kokhba</a>, killed.&nbsp;<a title="Judea (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judea_(Roman_province)">Judea</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Roman Syria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Syria">Syria</a>&nbsp;were combined into the single&nbsp;<a title="Roman province" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_province">province</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Syria Palaestina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria_Palaestina">Syria Palaestina</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td>25 February</td>

</tr>

<td><a title="AD 142" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AD_142">142</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The construction of the&nbsp;<a title="Antonine Wall" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antonine_Wall">Antonine Wall</a>&nbsp;at the northern border of&nbsp;<a title="Roman Britain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Britain">Britain</a>&nbsp;began.</td>

<td>7 March</td>
<td><a title="Antoninus Pius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antoninus_Pius">Antoninus</a>&nbsp;died. He was succeeded by&nbsp;<a title="Marcus Aurelius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius">Marcus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Lucius Verus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucius_Verus">Lucius Verus</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Carthage (238)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Carthage_(238)">Battle of Carthage (238)</a></em>: Forces loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Gordian I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordian_I">Gordian I</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Gordian II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordian_II">Gordian II</a>&nbsp;were defeated by the army of&nbsp;<a title="Capelianus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capelianus">Capelianus</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Roman governor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_governor">governor</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Numidia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numidia">Numidia</a>, who claimed fealty to&nbsp;<a title="Maximinus Thrax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximinus_Thrax">Maximinus</a>. Gordian II was killed. Gordian I committed suicide.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top">22 April</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;elected two senators,&nbsp;<a title="Pupienus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pupienus">Pupienus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Balbinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balbinus">Balbinus</a>, as joint rulers of the Empire.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Facing popular opposition to&nbsp;<a title="Pupienus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pupienus">Pupienus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Balbinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balbinus">Balbinus</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;gave&nbsp;<a title="Gordian I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordian_I">Gordian I's</a>&nbsp;young grandson&nbsp;<a title="Gordian III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordian_III">Gordian III</a>&nbsp;the title&nbsp;<a title="Caesar (title)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_(title)">Caesar</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>May</td>
<td><a title="Maximinus Thrax" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximinus_Thrax">Maximinus</a>&nbsp;was murdered with his son during a mutiny of the&nbsp;<a title="Legio II Parthica" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legio_II_Parthica">Legio II Parthica</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Aquileia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aquileia">Aquileia</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>29 July</td>
<td><a title="Pupienus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pupienus">Pupienus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Balbinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balbinus">Balbinus</a>&nbsp;were tortured and murdered by the&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian Guard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_Guard">Praetorian Guard</a>&nbsp;in their barracks.</td>

<td><a title="244" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/244">244</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Misiche" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Misiche">Battle of Misiche</a></em>: The&nbsp;<a title="Sasanian Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>&nbsp;decisively defeated a Roman force at Misiche, near modern&nbsp;<a title="Fallujah" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fallujah">Fallujah</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Gordian III" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gordian_III">Gordian III</a>&nbsp;was killed, probably by a fellow Roman. He was succeeded by&nbsp;<a title="Philip the Arab" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_the_Arab">Philip the Arab</a>, the&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian prefect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_prefect">prefect</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian Guard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_Guard">Praetorian Guard</a>, who was forced to cede&nbsp;<a title="Mesopotamia (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia_(Roman_province)">Mesopotamia</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)">Armenia</a>&nbsp;to the Sasanian Empire.</td>
</tr>

<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian Guard" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_Guard">Praetorian Guard</a>&nbsp;elected their&nbsp;<a title="Praetorian prefect" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Praetorian_prefect">prefect</a>&nbsp;<a title="Carus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carus">Carus</a>&nbsp;ruler of Rome.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Aurelius Probus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius_Probus">Probus</a>&nbsp;was assassinated.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Carus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carus">Carus</a>&nbsp;gave his sons&nbsp;<a title="Carinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carinus">Carinus</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Numerian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerian">Numerian</a>&nbsp;the title&nbsp;<a title="Caesar (title)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_(title)">Caesar</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="283" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/283">283</a></td>

<td><a title="Numerian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerian">Numerian</a>&nbsp;died.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>20 November</td>
<td>Roman forces in the east elected the&nbsp;<a title="Roman consul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_consul">consul</a>&nbsp;<a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;their ruler and proclaimed him&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="285" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/285">285</a></td>
<td>July</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of the Margus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Margus">Battle of the Margus</a></em>: Forces loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;defeated&nbsp;<a title="Carinus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carinus">Carinus</a>&nbsp;in battle on the&nbsp;<a title="Morava (river)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morava_(river)">Morava</a>. Carinus was killed.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;gave&nbsp;<a title="Maximian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximian">Maximian</a>&nbsp;the title&nbsp;<a title="Caesar (title)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_(title)">Caesar</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em><a title="Carausian Revolt" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carausian_Revolt">Carausian Revolt</a></em>: The naval commander&nbsp;<a title="Carausius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carausius">Carausius</a>&nbsp;declared himself&nbsp;<a title="Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emperor">emperor</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Roman Britain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Britain">Britain</a>&nbsp;and northern&nbsp;<a title="Gaul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaul">Gaul</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2 April</td>
<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;proclaimed&nbsp;<a title="Maximian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximian">Maximian</a>&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">west</a>, ruling himself as&nbsp;<em>augustus</em>&nbsp;of the east.</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan="3" valign="top"><a title="293" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/293">293</a></td>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;established the&nbsp;<a title="Tetrarchy" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tetrarchy">Tetrarchy</a>, appointing&nbsp;<a title="Constantius Chlorus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantius_Chlorus">Constantius Chlorus</a>&nbsp;to hold the office of&nbsp;<a title="Caesar (title)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_(title)">Caesar</a>&nbsp;under&nbsp;<a title="Maximian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximian">Maximian</a>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">west</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Galerius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galerius">Galerius</a>&nbsp;to hold the title under himself in the east.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><em>Carausian Revolt</em>:&nbsp;<a title="Constantius Chlorus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantius_Chlorus">Constantius Chlorus</a>&nbsp;conquered&nbsp;<a title="Carausius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carausius">Carausius's</a>&nbsp;<a title="Gaul" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaul">Gallic</a>&nbsp;territories.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Carausius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carausius">Carausius</a>&nbsp;was murdered by his finance minister&nbsp;<a title="Allectus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allectus">Allectus</a>, who replaced him as&nbsp;<a title="Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emperor">emperor</a>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Roman Britain" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Britain">Britain</a>.</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<a title="Edict on Maximum Prices" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_on_Maximum_Prices">Edict on Maximum Prices</a>, reforming the currency and setting price ceilings on a number of goods.</td>

<td><a title="303" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/303">303</a></td>
<td>24 February</td>
<td><em><a title="Diocletianic Persecution" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletianic_Persecution">Diocletianic Persecution</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;issued his first edict against&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christians</a>, calling for the destruction of Christian holy books and places of worship and stripping Christians of their government positions and political rights.</td>
</tr>

<td><a title="305" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/305">305</a></td>
<td>1 May</td>
<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Maximian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximian">Maximian</a>&nbsp;abdicated.&nbsp;<a title="Constantius Chlorus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantius_Chlorus">Constantius</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Galerius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galerius">Galerius</a>&nbsp;were elevated to&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augusti</a></em>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">west</a>&nbsp;and east. Galerius appointed&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Flavius Valerius Severus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flavius_Valerius_Severus">Flavius Valerius Severus</a>&nbsp;<a title="Caesar (title)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesar_(title)">Caesar</a>&nbsp;in the west and&nbsp;<a title="Maximinus II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximinus_II">Maximinus II</a>&nbsp;Caesar in the east.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="4" valign="top"><a title="306" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/306">306</a></td>
<td>25 July</td>
<td><a title="Constantius Chlorus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantius_Chlorus">Constantius</a>&nbsp;died at&nbsp;<a title="Eboracum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eboracum">Eboracum</a>. By his dying wish, his troops acclaimed his son&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>

<td>&nbsp;</td>

He took the title&nbsp;<em>princeps invictus</em>, undefeated prince.</td>
</tr>

Many of his soldiers defected to&nbsp;<a title="Maxentius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxentius">Maxentius</a>&nbsp;and he was forced to flee.</td>

</tr>

<td><a title="Diocletian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diocletian">Diocletian</a>&nbsp;died, possibly from suicide.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a title="312" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/312">312</a></td>
<td>28 October</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of the Milvian Bridge" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Milvian_Bridge">Battle of the Milvian Bridge</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;had a vision of the&nbsp;<a title="Christian cross" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_cross">cross</a>&nbsp;appearing over the sun at the&nbsp;<a title="Ponte Milvio" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ponte_Milvio">Ponte Milvio</a>&nbsp;with the words "in this sign, conquer." His forces defeated and killed&nbsp;<a title="Maxentius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxentius">Maxentius</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td rowspan="4" valign="top"><a title="313" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/313">313</a></td>
<td>February</td>
<td><a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;issued the&nbsp;<a title="Edict of Milan" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edict_of_Milan">Edict of Milan</a>, providing for restitution to&nbsp;<a title="Christianity" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity">Christians</a>&nbsp;injured during the persecutions.</td>

</tr>

<td>30 April</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Tzirallum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Tzirallum">Battle of Tzirallum</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;defeated a vastly numerically superior force loyal to&nbsp;<a title="Maximinus II" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximinus_II">Maximinus</a>&nbsp;at modern&nbsp;<a title="&Ccedil;orlu" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%87orlu">&Ccedil;orlu</a>. <td><em><a title="Battle of Mardia" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Mardia">Battle of Mardia</a></em>: After a bloody battle, probably at modern&nbsp;<a title="Harmanli" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmanli">Harmanli</a>,&nbsp;<a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;retreated from contact with&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1 March</td>
<td><a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;recognized&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;as his superior, ceded all his territories outside of&nbsp;<a title="Thrace" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thrace">Thrace</a>, and agreed to depose and execute&nbsp;<a title="Valerius Valens" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valerius_Valens">Valerius Valens</a>, whom he had raised to&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>.</td>
</tr>

<td>3 July</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Adrianople (324)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Adrianople_(324)">Battle of Adrianople (324)</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;suffered a bloody defeat at the hands of&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;on the&nbsp;<a title="Maritsa" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maritsa">Maritsa</a>.</td>

<tr>
<td>18 September</td>
<td><em><a title="Battle of Chrysopolis" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Chrysopolis">Battle of Chrysopolis</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;dealt a decisive defeat to the remnants of&nbsp;<a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius's</a>&nbsp;army. Licinius surrendered.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="325" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/325">325</a></td>
<td>20 May</td>
<td><em><a title="First Council of Nicaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Council_of_Nicaea">First Council of Nicaea</a></em>: An&nbsp;<a title="Ecumenical council" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecumenical_council">ecumenical council</a>&nbsp;called by&nbsp;<a title="Constantine the Great" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great">Constantine the Great</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Nicaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicaea">Nicaea</a>&nbsp;opened which would establish the&nbsp;<a title="Nicene Creed" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicene_Creed">Nicene Creed</a>, asserting&nbsp;<a title="Jesus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesus">Jesus</a>&nbsp;to be equal to and of the same substance as&nbsp;<a title="God the Father" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God_the_Father">God the Father</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Licinius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licinius">Licinius</a>&nbsp;was executed.</td>
</tr>
<tr>

<td>17 January</td>
<td><a title="Theodosius I" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodosius_I">Theodosius the Great</a>&nbsp;died. His elder son&nbsp;<a title="Arcadius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arcadius">Arcadius</a>&nbsp;succeeded him as&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>&nbsp;in the eastern&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>. The young&nbsp;<a title="Honorius (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honorius_(emperor)">Honorius</a>&nbsp;became sole&nbsp;<em>augustus</em>&nbsp;in the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>&nbsp;under the regency of&nbsp;<em><a title="Magister militum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magister_militum">Magister militum</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Stilicho" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stilicho">Stilicho</a>.</td>

<td><a title="Leo I the Thracian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_I_the_Thracian">Leo the Thracian</a>&nbsp;appointed&nbsp;<a title="Julius Nepos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Nepos">Julius Nepos</a>, his nephew and&nbsp;<a title="Roman governor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_governor">governor</a>&nbsp;of&nbsp;<a title="Dalmatia (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalmatia_(Roman_province)">Dalmatia</a>, ruler of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>&nbsp;in opposition to&nbsp;<a title="Glycerius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glycerius">Glycerius</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>18 January</td>
<td><a title="Leo I the Thracian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_I_the_Thracian">Leo the Thracian</a>&nbsp;died. He was succeeded by his grandson&nbsp;<a title="Leo II (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_II_(emperor)">Leo II (emperor)</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>9 February</td>
<td><a title="Zeno (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)">Zeno (emperor)</a>&nbsp;became co-<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>&nbsp;with his young son&nbsp;<a title="Leo II (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_II_(emperor)">Leo II</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>July</td>
<td><a title="Julius Nepos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Nepos">Nepos</a>&nbsp;deposed&nbsp;<a title="Glycerius" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glycerius">Glycerius</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>17 November</td>
<td><a title="Leo II (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_II_(emperor)">Leo II</a>&nbsp;died, possibly after being poisoned by his mother&nbsp;<a title="Ariadne (empress)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ariadne_(empress)">Ariadne (empress)</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td rowspan="5" valign="top"><a title="475" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/475">475</a></td>
<td>January</td>
<td><a title="Zeno (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)">Zeno</a>&nbsp;was forced to flee&nbsp;<a title="Constantinople" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople">Constantinople</a>&nbsp;for his homeland&nbsp;<a title="Isauria" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isauria">Isauria</a>&nbsp;in the face of a popular revolt.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>9 January</td>
<td><a title="Basiliscus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basiliscus">Basiliscus</a>, brother of&nbsp;<a title="Leo I the Thracian" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leo_I_the_Thracian">Leo the Thracian's</a>&nbsp;widow&nbsp;<a title="Verina" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verina">Verina</a>, was acclaimed&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>&nbsp;by the&nbsp;<a title="Byzantine Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Senate">Byzantine Senate</a>.</em></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td><a title="Julius Nepos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Nepos">Nepos</a>&nbsp;appointed&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orestes_(father_of_Romulus_Augustulus)">Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)</a>&nbsp;<em><a title="Magister militum" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magister_militum">Magister militum</a></em>&nbsp;and&nbsp;<a title="Commander-in-chief" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman</a>&nbsp;military.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>28 August</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" title="Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orestes_(father_of_Romulus_Augustulus)">Orestes</a>&nbsp;took control of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman</a>&nbsp;capital&nbsp;<a title="Ravenna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ravenna">Ravenna</a>, forcing&nbsp;<a title="Julius Nepos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Nepos">Nepos</a>&nbsp;to flee to&nbsp;<a title="Dalmatia (Roman province)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalmatia_(Roman_province)">Dalmatia</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>31 October</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" title="Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orestes_(father_of_Romulus_Augustulus)">Orestes</a>&nbsp;declared his young son&nbsp;<a title="Romulus Augustulus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus">Romulus Augustulus</a>&nbsp;<em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus (honorific)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)">augustus</a></em>&nbsp;of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan="5" valign="top"><a title="476" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/476">476</a></td>
<td>August</td>

</tr>
<tr>
<td>23 August</td>
<td><a title="Germanic peoples" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_peoples">Germanic</a>&nbsp;<em><a title="Foederati" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foederati">foederati</a></em>&nbsp;under the command of the&nbsp;<a title="General officer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_officer">general</a>&nbsp;<a title="Odoacer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odoacer">Odoacer</a>&nbsp;renounced&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman</a>&nbsp;authority and declared Odoacer their&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>28 August</td>
<td><a title="Odoacer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odoacer">Odoacer</a>&nbsp;captured and executed&nbsp;<a class="mw-redirect" title="Orestes (father of Romulus Augustulus)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orestes_(father_of_Romulus_Augustulus)">Orestes</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Piacenza" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piacenza">Piacenza</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>4 September</td>
<td><a title="Odoacer" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odoacer">Odoacer</a>&nbsp;conquered the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman</a>&nbsp;capital&nbsp;<a title="Ravenna" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ravenna">Ravenna</a>, forced&nbsp;<a title="Romulus Augustulus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romulus_Augustulus">Romulus</a>&nbsp;to abdicate and declared himself&nbsp;<a title="King" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King">king</a>&nbsp;of Italy.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Roman Senate" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Senate">Senate</a>&nbsp;sent&nbsp;<a title="Zeno (emperor)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeno_(emperor)">Zeno</a>&nbsp;the imperial regalia of the&nbsp;<a title="Western Roman Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.</td>
</tr>

<td rowspan="2" valign="top"><a title="1204" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1204">1204</a></td>
<td>13 April</td>
<td><em><a class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Constantinople (1204)" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(1204)">Siege of Constantinople (1204)</a></em>:&nbsp;<a title="Fourth Crusade" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fourth_Crusade">Fourth Crusaders</a>&nbsp;breached and sacked&nbsp;<a title="Constantinople" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, deposed the&nbsp;<em><a title="Basileus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basileus">basileus</a></em>&nbsp;<a title="Alexios V Doukas" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexios_V_Doukas">Alexios V Doukas</a>&nbsp;and established the&nbsp;<a title="Latin Empire" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_Empire">Latin Empire</a>&nbsp;under their leader&nbsp;<a title="Baldwin I, Latin Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baldwin_I,_Latin_Emperor">Baldwin I, Latin Emperor</a>&nbsp;as&nbsp;<a title="Latin Emperor" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_Emperor">Latin Emperor</a>.&nbsp;<a title="Theodore I Laskaris" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodore_I_Laskaris">Theodore I Laskaris</a>&nbsp;was acclaimed&nbsp;<em>basileus</em>&nbsp;but forced to flee with his court to establish the&nbsp;<a title="Empire of Nicaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Nicaea">Empire of Nicaea</a>&nbsp;at&nbsp;<a title="Nicaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicaea">Nicaea</a>.</td>

<td>The&nbsp;<a title="Empire of Nicaea" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Nicaea">Nicaean</a>&nbsp;ruler&nbsp;<a title="Michael VIII Palaiologos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_VIII_Palaiologos">Michael VIII Palaiologos</a>&nbsp;conquered&nbsp;<a title="Constantinople" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople">Constantinople</a>&nbsp;.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>15 August</td>
<td><a title="Michael VIII Palaiologos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_VIII_Palaiologos">Michael</a>&nbsp;was crowned&nbsp;<em><a title="Basileus" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basileus">basileus</a></em>&nbsp;in&nbsp;<a title="Constantinople" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople">Constantinople</a>&nbsp;along with his infant son&nbsp;<a title="Andronikos II Palaiologos" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andronikos_II_Palaiologos">Andronikos II Palaiologos</a>.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
